DJIBOUTI: INTERNATIONAL ROAD CORRIDOR REHABILITATION PROJECT
CONSTRUCTION MANAGEMENT
Terms of Reference
A.  BACKGROUND
1. The Government of Djibouti (GD) has requested assistance from the International Development
Association (IDA), for a program of emergency road repair of some sections of the national road to
Ethiopia. The Ministry of Equipment and Transport (MOET) will be responsible for the works to be
carried out by contractors selected through National Competitive Bidding (NCB) procedures, goods
contracts and some use of MOET equipment and forces. The works and goods will be supervised for
quality assurance and contractual compliance by international supervisors under contract to MOET.
2. The works to be carried out include emergency repairs on some 102 km of Dikhil - Galafi, (Ethiopian
Border), and 86 km of emergency repairs, pothole repairs and maintenance works in the Arta turnoff to
Dikhil section. The repair works consist of reconstruction of damaged and deteriorated sub-bases and
base courses, placement of a double layer of surface treatment, repair of minor drainage structures and
concrete drifts, shoulder and slope work and pot hole repairs. Maintenance works on the entire Djibouti -
Galafi road will be initiated under this project. The implementation period of the whole project will be
four years with the construction period lasting the first twelve months and the institutional strengthening
and maintenance period extending over the next thirty-six months.
B.    OBJECTIVE AND SCOPE OF WORKS
3.    The objectives of the assignment are to provide construction management services through the
pre-construction, construction and start of the maintenance phase. The construction manager's main goal
is to ensure that the work is properly installed in accordance with the project schedule.
4.    On behalf of the GD, the MOET proposes to invite technical and financial proposals from short
listed consultants to manage the installation of repair works for GD. The Construction Manager (CM) will
select the contracting methodology, including, but not limited to, competitively bid contracts for works
and goods, and use of the MOET equipment and personnel to perform works, and maintenance contracts.
The manager will use previously prepared bidding documents, modified if needed to conform with
constracting methods proposed by the CM, perform bid evaluations and award construction contracts with
the concurrence of GD. Supervision of the works will be by other consultants who will report directly to
GD. The manager will also select and manage GD equipment, personnel and a repair shop at Dikhil. This
will in effect create a force account unit to allow the manager options in carrying out the repair and
maintenance of the road. Details of the invitation/evaluation of proposals are given in the Request for
Proposal.
5.    The management team and man-months (m/m) for the management of all road works contracts,
should be proposed on the basis of the contracts' characteristics and construction periods. A preliminary
assessment is that the team would comprise at least, a Project Manager (with experience on construction,
repair and maintenance of national roads), a general field superintendent and a supervisor for the force
account unit. It is envisioned that equipment operators, mechanics, laborers, office staff and some field
survey staff is available from GD. The Consultant will indicate the number of GD staff support required
106



for the contract, and bidders are encouraged to visit MOET to determine staff resources likely to be
available prior to preparing bids.
C.    ENVIRONMENTAL AND SOCIAL REQUIREMENTS
6.    Mitigation Measures. The Environmental Management Plan (EMP) provides for instructions to
be given to the construction contractors for undertaking specific actions to support implementation of
portions of the Plan. For specifics refer to the EMP for the project which is available in English and in
French. The EMP supports the following:
(a)    Reduction of Potential Construction Impacts. Specific measures to reduce potential
construction impacts should be taken regarding the construction tenders, construction process
and contractor performance monitoring.
(b)    Management of Health and Safety issues. Specific measures to reduce construction period
worker health and safety issues should be taken regarding the construction tenders,
construction process and contractor performance monitoring.
(c)    As part of the maintenance program, the MOET will make certain that routine maintenance is
undertaken to keep water crossings clear of debris and that culverts are regularly cleared of
sediment and debris.
(d)    Regrading of material sites. The project would require the regrading of material collection
sites when extraction of materials is completed.
(e)    Cultural heritage. Provisions will be made for the services of an archaeologist from ISERST
to conduct on-site monitoring during major earth moving and materials collection, and
support implementation of archaeological "change find" procedures. In addition, specific
actions will be taken with respect to finding unrecorded graveyards and burial sites.
(f)    Local Employment. The project would work with local authorities, village chiefs and elders
in the project area to facilitate local employment by construction contractors.
(g)    Establishment of an HIV/AIDS Outreach Program. The project will support design and
implementation of an HIV/AIDS education and outreach program. This will be directed to
employees of the construction contractor, traveling industry, and permanent and temporary
residents of the project area.
7.    Measures for Design and Construction Contracts. The EMP includes the following mitigation
measures for construction tenders and construction contracts:
(a)    All construction contracts will include specific provisions concerning environmental,
health and safety measures.
(b)    Pre-Tender Conference. All pre-qualified contractors will be called to a pre-Tender
conference at which environmental issues of special interest or concern will be outlined.
This will include a review of the application of archaeological "chance find" procedures.
107



D.    DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES OF THE CONSTRUCTION MANAGER
8.    The construction manager will manage the works and admninister the works contracts and ensure
that contractual clauses whether related to quality or quantities of work, are carried out. The CM will
determine the most effective and economical way to implement the project.
9.    The CM will utilize plans and specifications furnished by GD, modified by the CM if needed to
conform with contracting methodology being used, and evaluate the most efficient and cost effective way
to implement the project by a combination of competitively bid contracts utilizing the private sector, by
materials purchase contracts of aggregates and other mnaterials, or by use of force account. The CM shall
also determine the number and size and type of contracts.
10.   The manager will ensure full compliance with the EMP in all aspects of the consultancy.
11.   Subsequent to receipt of the various bids the CM will evaluate the results and recommend award
or rejection.
12.   The CM will take the necessary measures to control the progress of works, and will make all
management decisions required for the satisfactory implementation of contracts in a timely manner.
However, after contracts are awarded, the Manager will seek approval of the GD to:
issue any variation order with financial implications, except in an emergency situation, as
reasonably determined by the CM;
-     issue variation in work quantities;
-     sanction additional items, sums or costs;
-     approve or sublet any part of the works; and
-     approve any extension of the time for completion.
13.   The Manager will carry out the following tasks:
(a)    Establish lines of communication and develop working procedures with the Djiboutian
Project Coordinator, who will be based in Djibouti City;
(b)   Include Project Coordinator in weekly staff meetings;
(c)    Mutually agree with the Project Coordinator on assignment of special areas of
responsibility to that office;
(d)    Develop a strategy to implement the work including works and goods contracts and force
account;
(e)   Issue the order to commence the works;
(f)    Manage the civil works and goods contracts;
(g)    Approve the works contractor's program of work;
(h)    Ensure that traffic operational safety is met before conmmencing the works;
108



(i)    Monitor progress of the work. If progress is not satisfactory, take necessary actions,
including supplementing or replacing the contractor's forces with force account personnel
and equipment;
(j)    Develop a force account unit capable of performing some works and all maintenance
works for the road;
(k)    Verify the work upon completion of the contracts;
(1)   Initiate a three year maintenance contract;
(m)   Monitor the works at the start of the maintenance period; and
(n)    advise MOET on all matters related to the execution of the contracts including providing
advise on Contractor's claims.
E.    DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES OF THE GENERAL SUPERINTENDENT
14.   The main responsibilities of the General Superintendent are:
(a)    Manage the performance of works in all aspects in the field including: ensuring that the
civil works contractors are installing critical parts of the work on time; ensuring
materials are delivered and produced on time; and that enough resources are in place to
complete the project according to schedule;
(b)    Maintain a daily presence in the field and take whatever measures are necessary to ensure
that schedule is met. This will range from giving directions to the works contractors, to
giving priority to certain parts of the work, to supplementing or replacing the contractors'
forces if they are unable or unwilling to perform;
(c)    Supervise the contractors in all matters concerning safety and care of the works, and
direct operations in case of an emergency situation affecting the safety of life, of the
works, or adjoining property;
(d)    Assign work to the force account manager and ensure proper interfacing with other
contractors;
(e)    Supervise the production of aggregates and other materials and ensure that the materials
are produced according to specification and schedule;
(f)    Supervise the startup of the maintenance program in the field carry out such duties, as
may be delegated in writing from the Construction Manager, in fulfilling the
terms of the contract.
F.    DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES OF THE FORCE ACCOUNT MANAGER
15.   The role of the Force Account Manager primarily is that of a field person supervising Force
Account operations. Initially, his role will be establishing a Force Account organization supported by a
reliable equipment capability. The main responsibilities of the Force Account Manager are:
109



(a)    Overall management of the force account personnel, plant and equipment;
(b)    Set up an equipment repair shop in Dikhil and select capable mechanics to install needed
repair parts and to keep the equipment operational;
(c)    Train operators to properly and skillfully operate the equipment;
(d)    Ensure that the repair shop is stocked with enough normal shop supplies and parts subject
to frequent replacement, to ensure no disruption to project schedule;
(e)    Train a labor force in road maintenance activities such as pot hole repairs, pavement
sealing, road side cleanup, sign installation and repair, installation of pavement markings,
etc.;
(f)    Set up system to keep track of actual equipment usage, down time and standby time and
repair costs;
(g)    Establish an equipment maintenance schedule;
(h)    Prepare cost estimates for performance of road repair works undertaken by the force
account group;
(i)    Establish an annual budget for the force account group;
(j)    Train Djiboutian counterpart to assume role of force account manager by the end of the
consultancy period; and
(k)    Carry out such duties, as may be delegated in writing from the construction manager,
under the terms of the Contract.
G.    OBLIGATIONS OF THE CONSTRUCTION MANAGER AND THE CLIENT
16.   The construction manager shall provide additional key expatriate staff personnel as envisioned in
the manager's plan of execution. This may include technical personnel such as cost engineers, an
accountant/office manager and field superintendents. However, the construction manager should utilize to
the fullest extent, staff of the MOET, including engineers, book keepers, secretaries, field survey, etc., all
of whom will be made available to the manager by MOET at no cost.
17.   MOET will make available its equipment yard in Dikhil for contract headquarters for the
construction manager and supervising engineer. The supervision engineer must establish headquarters in
Dikhil and may utilize existing facilities which will be- repaired and upgraded for the use of both the CM
and supervising engineer. The need for additional facilities in other locations will be determined and
provided by the supervision engineer.
18.   At Dikhil, the CM shall be responsible for providing furnished office and residential
accommodation (e.g. pre-fabricated buildings, porta-cabins) and arranging supporting infrastructur
facilities (water, electricity, sewage, etc), office equipment (computers, photocopiers, fax, e-mail, etc) and
transportation.

19.   The use of existing laboratory facilities, field test devices and testing equipment will be available

20.   The manager will provide his office furniture and supplies, computer systems, telephones, faxes,

21.   The manager will furnish six vehicles to the project, three for the manager's use and three for the

roads administration.

obligations.
24.   Any reports, documents, drawings, and in general, any available information related to the design
and execution of the works shall be made available by MOET to the construction manager.
25.   All documentation related to the works is, and will remain after completion of works, MOET's
property. The construction manager can not use or dispose of this documentation without previous
consent.

forth in this TOR.

DJIBOUTI: INTERNATIONAL ROAD CORRIDOR REHABILITATION PROJECT
SUPERVISION OF CONSTRUCTION WORKS
Terms of Reference
A.  BACKGROUND
1.    The Government of Djibouti (GD) has requested assistance from the International Development
Association (IDA), for a program of emergency road repair of some sections of the national road to
Ethiopia via Galafi. The Ministry of Transport (MET) will be responsible for the works to be carried out
by contractors selected through National Competitive Bidding (NCB) procedures, works and goods
contracts and some use of MET plant, equipment and personnel. The works and goods contracts will be
supervised for quality assurance and contractual compliance by international supervisors under contract to
MET.
B.  SCOPE OF WORKS
2.    The works to be carried out include emergency repairs to some 100 km of the Dikhil - Galafi
road to the Ethiopian border, and emergency repairs and maintenance works to the 88 km Arta turnoff to
Dikhil section. The repair works consist of reconstruction of damaged and deteriorated sub-bases and
base courses, placement of a double layer of surface treatment, repair of minor drainage structures and
concrete drifts, shoulder and slope works and pothole repairs. Maintenance works on the entire Djibouti-
Galafi road will be initiated under this project.
3.    The implementation period of the repair works will be approximately 9 months with substantial
completion scheduled within the first 7 months. The defects liability period will be 12 months after
completion of the works with a maintenance period extending for a further 24 months.
C.    OBJECTIVES AND SCOPE OF THE ASSIGNMENT
4.    On behalf of the GD, the MET proposes to invite technical and financial proposals from short
listed consultants to provide pre-construction and construction supervision services. The scope of the
services will include, but not necessarily be limited to, the following:
(a)    verification, adjustment where necessary, and assumption of responsibility for the
following items prepared previously by specialist consultants:
-     an outline pavement design(s) to bituminous standard and typical cross-sections
for the rehabilitation of the road to carry the projected traffic for a relatively
short life span of 5 years; and
-     the scope of repairs of minor drainage structures along the road consisting
of concrete box culverts and Irish crossings.
(b)    supervising the works contracts on behalf of the client with regard to quality assurance
and contractual compliance including, but not necessarily limited to, the following
activities:
-      supervising the construction works contracts to ensure that contractual clauses,
whether related to quality or quantities of work, are respected;
112



-     undertaking the necessary quality control of works,
-     making all engineering decisions-including improvement of designs, if
necessary-required for the good implementation of the contract;
-     making amendments to or extensions of the sources of materials identified
previously by the specialist consultants to meet the necessary production targets.
5.    The supervision team would be proposed by the consultants on the basis of the contracts'
characteristics and construction periods and would include at least a Chief Supervision Engineer and one
Supervision Engineer. The personnel proposed to be used by the consultants will require to have
extensive experience of road construction supervision as well as a sound knowledge of materials testing
and utilization in pavements as well as thorough familiarity of quality control procedures in environments
similar to that prevailing in the project area. The consultant will indicate the number of GD support staff
required for the project (surveyors, soils technicians, inspectors, etc).
D.    DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES OF THE SUPERVISION CONSULTANT
6.    The duties and responsibilities of the Chief Supervision Engineer will include, but not necessarily
be limited to, the following:
(a)   supervising the civil works contracts, approve the materials and quality of the works in
accordance with the Contract;
(b)    providing support to the archaeologist from ISERST for undertaking on-site work during
major earth moving and materials collecting activities;
(c)    providing support to MET and ISERST in implementation of archaeological "chance
find" procedures
(d)    ensuring compliance with the various mitigation measures and monitoring actions
contained in the Environmental Management Plan;
(e)   reviewing the Contractor's Program of Work and verifying and approving the source of
materials;
(f)    approving the Contractor's working drawings including variations thereof;
(g)    approving the setting out of the works and give instructions to the Contractor in this
regard;
(h)    ordering tests of materials and completed works and ordering the removal of improper or
substandard works;
(i)    ensuring that traffic operational safety is adequate before commencing the works and
issuing any work plan or drawing in that respect;
(j)   inspecting the works during the maintenance period, and issuing the maintenance
certificate in consultation with client;
(k)    with the prior approval of the client:
7.    The main responsibilities of the Supervision Engineers will include, but not necessarily be limited
to, the following:
113



(a)   inspecting the performance of works in compliance with specifications;
(b)    ordering, supervising or performing tests on materials and approving or disapproving the
contractor's plant and equipment; and
(c)   supervising the contractor in all matters concerning safety and care of the works, and
directing operations in case of an emergency situation affecting the safety of life, of the
works, or adjoining property.
E.    OBLIGATIONS OF THE CLIENT
8.    Any reports, documents, drawings, and in general, any available information related to the design
and execution of the works shall be made available by the Client to the Consultant.
9.    A Project Director has been appointed by the Client to liase with the supervision consultants, the
Construction Management Consultant and client bodies on all matters related to the execution of the
works.
10.   The MET will make available its equipment yard in Dikhil as site for the project headquarters for
the construction manager and supervising engineers. The need for additional facilities in other locations
will be determined and provided by the supervision engineer.
11.   Laboratory facilities and field and laboratory testing equipment will be provided by the CM.
F.    OBLIGATIONS OF THE SUPERVISION CONSULTANT
12.   All documentation related to the works is, and will remain after completion of works, the Client's
property. The Supervision Engineers can not use or dispose of this documentation without previous
consent.
13.   The Supervision Engineer shall carry out at least three inspection visits during the one-year
Defects Liability contractual period to be established for the maintenance of works after completion.
G.  REPORTS AND DOCUMENTS
14.   The Supervision Engineer shall furnish to client with the following reporting and documents in
English and French:
(a)    Provide sections for the Construction Management Consultant's monthly Progress
Reports relating to the quality control aspects, the date of the agreement signed between
the Contractor and client for construction of works, and ending at the end of the month in
which the issue of the provisional completion certificate, i.e. the starting date of the one-
year contractual maintenance period, takes place; and
(b)    At the time of the final completion of the works, provide sections for the Construction
Management Consultant's completion report as appropriate.

DJIBOUTI: INTERNATIONAL ROAD CORRIDOR REHABILITATION PROJECT
PREPARA TION OFPA VEMENT DESIGN CONCEPTS
Terms of Reference
A.  BACKGROUND
1.    Djibouti currently serves as the primary transit port for landlocked Ethiopia following the
outbreak of armed conflict between Ethiopia and Eritrea in 1998. Assab, on the Eritrean coast, formerly
played this role, but with the sudden shift in 1998 of traffic from Assab Port to Djibouti Port, the 20 year
old road connection between Djibouti Port and the Addis-Assab Road (via Dikhil and Galafi, see attached
map) was suddenly required to carry a level of heavy-vehicle traffic it was neither designed for nor in a
condition to carry. The lack of regular maintenance within Djibouti has contributed to the accelerated
deterioration of this 188 km road section, which originally had a double surface dressing over a natural
gravel base/sub-base. Portions of the road are presently disintegrating, posing a risk of complete failure
on long sections. On the 102 km section closest to the border, all bituminous surfacing has either been
destroyed by traffic or scarified to improve rideability, and the road is kept passable by occasional
grading. On the 86 km road section closest to Djibouti city (Arta turnoff to Dikhil) about 18 km has
recently been repaired by a local contractor. However, this work is very short term and already requires
maintenance repairs. The rest, partly in a state of rapid deterioration, is causing accidents and is slowing
down truck traffic significantly. Maintaining this 188 km road link is critical to Djibouti Port's ability to
serve the Ethiopian traffic, and remain competitive in the long-run.
2.    Recently the Djibouti Government requested the International Development Association (IDA) to
assist in financing limited, but adequate, rehabilitation of the road pavement as well as emergency repairs
to drainage structures, and to ensure that the 188 km road section will be well maintained thereafter. The
objective of this rehabilitation project is to secure unhampered and continued road access between
Djibouti Port and Ethiopia for the next five years, and thereby guarantee that the existing lifeline to
Addis-Ababa -- through which crucial Ethiopian agricultural imports (e.g. fertilizers), as well as
international famine-relief shipments must pass -- remains functional. During this 5-year period an Addis
Ababa-Djibouti City long-term corridor improvement scheme is being developed, assessed, and
implemented by the Ethiopian and Djibouti governments with assistance from the European Union which
is expected to provide the long term improvements to the corridor. However, during this period, it is clear
that the Djibouti-Galafi road cannot remain in its present deteriorated state without doing serious harm to
the economies of both Djibouti and Ethiopia.
3.    The Ministry of Equipment and Transport is responsible for the national road network. As part of
an effort in 'fast-tracking' the implementation of the IDA-supported pavement rehabilitation project, the
services of a highly experienced agency/firm would be required to assist in the preparation of pavement
rehabilitation design concepts for the two sections on either side of the Dikhil township. The World Bank
has secured grant funds from the Japanese Policy and Human Resource Development Fund (PHRD) for
this purpose.
B.    OBJECTIVES OF THE ASSIGNMENT
4.    The emergency nature of this assignment requires the selected agency/firm to respond quickly in
preparing proposals for providing the services, as well as to mobilize the team to carry out the services as
a matter of urgency. The overall objective is to prepare concept designs of the necessary rehabilitation
work sufficient to be able to prepare typical tender documents for some or all of the works while the
Government goes through a normal selection process to procure the services of a supervision consultant
115



to verify, adjust and take responsibility for the design and subsequent implementation of works. This
would save valuable time. The services described below should ideally commence on approximately l't
May 2000 and have to be completed as soon as possible, and no later than 30' June 2000.
5.     Against the background context of the project setting outlined above, the detailed objectives of
the assignment are to:
(a)    Produce appropriate outline pavement design(s) and typical cross-sections for the
rehabilitation of the road to carry the projected traffic for a relatively short life span of 5
years;
(b)    Provide alternative, feasible pavement designs to a bituminous surfacing standard which
would be adequate for the relatively short life span of 5-6 years for the rehabilitation
works and which would serve substantially as an intermediate component of the longer
term corridor improvement scheme;
(c)    Assess the sources of suitable materials (particularly aggregates and water) to meet
production targets that would facilitate implementation in a short time as practically
possible, given all constraints locally;
(d)    Assess the scope of temporary repairs of minor drainage structures along the road
consisting of concrete box culverts and Irish crossings; and
(e)    Work with the contracts specialist (procured separately), providing technical input in the
process of preparing bidding documents.
C.  SCOPE OF WORKS
6.     The services of a soils/materials/pavement specialist are required to assist the Project
Implementation Unit (PIU) of the Ministry of Equipment and Transport in implementing the emergency
rehabilitation works. Information on the road at the time of its construction in 1976 in terms of soils and
materials investigations and laboratory test results, cross-sections, pavement design, longitudinal plans
and profiles, geometric information, bills of quantities, cost estimates, etc are all available and will
provide a valuable source of background informnation to the specialist. With reference to the background
information already available on the road, the anticipated scope of work shall include, but not necessarily
be limited, to the following:
(a)    Produce alternative, feasible pavement designs and typical cross-sections for the
rehabilitation of the road to a bituminous surfacing standard that would be adequate to
carry the projected traffic for a relatively short life span of 5-6 years and would also
serve substantially as a component of the longer term corridor improvement scheme;
(b)    Locate suitable materials (particularly aggregates and water) in sufficient quantities along
the project corridor for use in the works;
(c)    Produce appropriate specifications for the materials proposed for use in works and for the
installation requirements;
(d)    Produce a Bill of Quantities for the entire length of the road based on the typical cross
sections;
(e)    Produce cost estimates for the works;
(f)    Produce drawings which, as a minimum, shall include typical road cross sections
116



showing limits, character and dimensions of the repaired roadway. Original plans of road
alignment and profile and details of standard construction features shall be reproduced for
inclusion in this contract by the PIU, if available;
(g)    Liaise with hydrology specialists undertaking work for the European Union-financed pre-
feasibility study of the transport corridor, to both assess the scope of temporary repairs of
minor drainage structures along the road consisting of concrete box culverts and Irish
crossings, and recommend earth borrowing procedures which are the least disruptive to
natural water flows. Liaise with the contracts specialist as required in obtaining water
information through the procurement of equipment, test devices or other resources.
Procurement of these services will be a reimbursable cost to the consultant to a maximum
limit of US$10,000.00; and
(h)    Liaise with the contracts specialist to ensure that the works requirements (specifications,
quantities, drawings, etc) are fully accounted for in the contract documents.
7.     Qualifications and Experience. The candidates (two) must hold at least a MSc degree related to
soils/materials/pavements with at least twenty years of experience, at least 10 of which should be in
environments similar to that prevailing in the project environment in Djibouti.
D.    GENERAL CONDITIONS OF THE ASSIGNMENT
8.    During the currency of the assignment:
(a)   the consultant shall:
(i)    determine the other technical services required to ensure timely completion of its
work;
(ii)   provide those services including, but not limited to, field surveys, laboratory and
field testing. Such services will be cost reimbursable to the consultants upon
receipt of invoices submitted by the consultants to a maximum limit of
US$10,000.00;
(iii)   perform the assignment in offices provided at no cost by the Roads Department
and shall keep the Roads Department informed of the progress on the
assignment;
(iv)   be responsible for local transport, accommodation, computers, local and
intemational calls and photo copying and printing; and
(v)    either be able to communicate with the PIU staff in French or have the services
of a French language interpreter, whose cost will be the consultants
responsibility.
E.    OUTPUTS OF THE ASSIGNMENT
9.    Interim Report: One month after the commencement of the assignment, the consultant shall
furnish the PIU with an interim report, indicating:
117



(a)  proposed technical solutions to the road rehabilitation and the basis thereof;
(b)  typical cross-sections and limits of the sections;
(c) preliminary conclusions on the sources, quality and quantity of water and
aggregates; and
(d)  preliminary estimates of cost of the rehabilitation works.
10.   The interim report will, in effect, be a status report of the interim conclusions of the assignment
and is intended as a status report for the information of the PIU. It is anticipated that the PIU will provide
comments leading to approval of this report within 4 days of receipt from the consultant.
11.   The interim report will be produced on computer diskette in both English and French. Five hard
copies will be produced in French and two copies in English.
12.   Final Report: Within two months after the commencement of the assignment, the consultant
shall furnish the PIU with a final report. It will include final conclusions and recommendations for all
issues covered in the interim report.
13.   The final report will be produced on diskette in French and English. In addition, five hard copies
will be produced in French and two in English. Drawings and plans will be provided in electronic or hard
copy format for bidding purposes.
G.    PAYMENTS
14.   This assignment is funded by the Japanese Government through a PHRD grant to be made
available to Djibouti and to be administered by the World Bank. The World Bank has been authorized by
the Djibouti Government to act as the implementing agency for this assignment to speed up the execution
of services and, consequently, the selection process, contract negotiation and award. Contractual
payments will be the responsibility of the World Bank. However, the firm or agency selected for this
assignment has to carry out the services in close collaboration with the PIU staff as the actual client of the
services.
15.   The lump sum contract amount will be paid as follows:
* 20% down payment upon contract signature
* 30% payment upon submittal of interim reports
* 30% payment upon submittal of the final report and documents
* 20% payment upon approval of final reports and documents the Roads Department.
H.  COMMENCEMENT AND DURATION OF ASSIGNMENT
16.   The assignment will commence around June 15 2000 and will have a duration of no more than 6
- 8 weeks.
118

the economies of both Djibouti and Ethiopia.
3.    The Ministry of Equipment and Transport is responsible for the national road network. As part of
an effort in 'fast-tracking' the implementation of the IDA-supported pavement rehabilitation project, the
services of a highly experienced individual would be required to assist in the preparation of typical
bidding documents for the two sections on either side of the Dikhil township. The World Bank has
secured grant funds from the Japanese Policy and Human Resource Development Fund (PHRD) for this
purpose.
B.    OBJECTIVES OF THE ASSIGNMENT

preparing proposals for providing the services, as well as to mobilize the team to carry out the services as
a matter of urgency. The overall objective is to prepare concept designs of the necessary rehabilitation
work sufficient to be able to prepare typical tender documents for some or all of the works while the
Government goes through a normal selection process to procure the services of a Construction Manager
119



to verify, adjust and take responsibility for the design, bidding documents and subsequent implementation
of works. This would save valuable time. The services described below should ideally commence on
approximately June 15, 2000, or earlier, and have to be completed as soon as possible, and no later than
July 31, 2000. The Contract Specialist will have to work closely with the consultant preparing typical
pavement designs and identifying materials sources (TRL).
5.     Against the background context of the project setting outlined above, the primary objective of the
assignment is to prepare typical bidding documents to facilitate an urgent completion of the works as well
as a proposed program for the execution of the works, including the number of works and goods contracts
and force account operations as appropriate.
C.  SCOPE OF WORKS
6.     A Contracts Specialist is required to assist the Project Implementation Unit (PIU) of the Ministry
of Equipment and Transport. The scope of work shall include, but not necessarily be limited, to the
following:
(a)    Work with the materials specialist (from TRL) to prepare typical bid documents for the
works and goods contracts to be executed under the credit.
(b)    Coordinate and manage the production of technical provisions, contract provisions, bid
data sheets, special conditions of contract, bills of quantities, bid forms and plans
necessary to obtain informed offers by potential bidders.
(c)    Review the technical provisions produced by the soils/materials/pavement specialists and
verify for clarity, completeness and compatibility with all the provisions of the contract.
(d)    Assist the soils/materials/pavement specialists in the selection of various technical
solutions by providing relative cost comparisons for methods under consideration.
Capability of local and regional contractors will be an essential consideration in the
selection of solutions.
7.     With respect to the rest of the works documents, the contracts specialist shall:
(a)    Prepare a preliminary and simplified bill of quantities and unit price schedule for each
contract.
(b)    Prepare a bid data sheet.
(c)    Prepare any special conditions of the contract.
(d)    Prepare the contract data sheet.
(e)    Assemble all contract documents into bid packages for approval by the Construction
Manager.
(f)    Prepare bid notices.
(g)    Assist the PIU in preparing a list of national and regional contractors who will be invited
to submit bids for national competitive bidding (NCB) of works and goods contracts.
(h)    Assist the PIUJ in establishing the minimum requirements for contractors to qualify for
NCB.
(i)    Assist the PIU in selecting the construction manager and supervision engineer (evaluation
of tender documents), quality control, supervision and training services for the project.
This part of the assignment will take place between July 10 and 31, 2000.

13.   Final Report: Within two months after the commencement of the assignment, the consultant
shall furnish the PIU with a final report. It will include final conclusions and recommendations for all
issues covered in the interim report.
14.   The final report will be produced on diskette in French and English. In addition, five hard copies
will be produced in French and two in English for distribution as under para 12. Typical bidding
documents, drawings and plans will be provided in electronic or hard copy format for bidding purposes.

15.   Along with the final report, the consultant shall furnish typical bid documents conforming to
World Bank procurement guidelines for the goods and works contracts prepared by the consultants. The
standardized bid documents will be produced on diskette in French and English. In addition, one hard
copy of each set of bid documents will be produced in French and one copy in English.

DJIBOUTI: INTERNATIONAL ROAD CORRIDOR REHABILITATION PROJECT
PREPARA TION OF BIDDING DOCUMENTS FOR SPARE PARTS
Terms of Reference
1.    The World Bank is preparing an emergency national road repair project for Djibouti and is
considering the use of Ministry owned equipment in the implementation of part of the project. As a
consequence, the Bank must know the cost to repair that part of the equipment fleet that is in good
condition, or can be made operable without complete overhaul or replacing all major systems. The
consultant will perform the consultancy in two phases:
2.    Prior to coming to Djibouti, the equipment specialist will review the list of Ministry owned
equipment in his home office and furnish the Government and the World Bank with an itemization of
repairs, and budget cost of repairs of usable equipment. With the exception of a few pieces, personnel
vehicles will not be included under this consultancy. The specialist's conclusions shall be furnished, in the
English and French language, to the Bank appraisal mission in Djibouti no later than May 31, 2000.
3.    The second phase will require the specialist to spend about three weeks in Djibouti. The
equipment specialist shall be on site approximately June 15, 2000, but in any event no later than fifteen
days after the commencement of the activities of the pavement and contracts specialists . The equipment
specialist shall liaise with these specialists, who will identify the equipment needed to complete parts of
the project on a force account basis.
4.    The equipment specialist next will inspect the fleet of equipment and select the best pieces for use
on the project. The specialist shall prepare an updated list of repairs and parts required to bring that, and
all the usable equipment, up to a level of good operating condition, and shall provide an updated cost
estimate. The specialist next shall prepare international shopping packages by category of parts, and/or
likely vendors of groups of parts, for the equipment intended for use on the project.
5.    The equipment specialist shall prepare a list setting forth the estimated salvage value of the
remaining equipment. That equipment may disposed of, if agreed by the client and the World Bank.
6.    Prior to completing the assignment (approximately July 31, 2000), the specialist shall prepare a
report, in the English and French languages, outlining recommendations and conclusions with respect to
the Ministry owned equipment in Djibouti.

DJIBOUTI: INTERNATIONAL ROAD CORRIDOR REHABILITATION PROJECT
TECHNICAL ASSISTANCE FOR THE DEVELOPMENT OF
TRADE RELA TEDSERVICES
Terms of Reference
A.  BACKGROUND
1.    The Port of Dj ibouti and the transport of goods from the port to its hinterland are, with the
possible exception of official development assistance, the mainstays of the economy of Djibouti. Its
strategic location on the Red Sea's international shipping routes, as well as in relation to its East African
neighbors, potentially make Djibouti an excellent entrepot for the region. For various reasons related to
geo-politics and infrastructure deficiencies, this potential has barely begun to be tapped. With
unemployment rates reportedly as high as 60 percent, development of the trade and transport sectors,
which could generate considerable employment in the local economy, is clearly a high priority for the
Government.
2.    Up until less than two years ago, the Port of Djibouti was the primary transshipment location for
international trade in the area. However, recent developments of new ports in the region have tended to
reduce Djibouti's role in the transshipment of international trade cargoes. In early 1998, the ports of Aden
in Yemen and Salalah in Oman opened large, modern, deepwater facilities, and major shipping lines are
now beginning to shift their transshipment business from Djibouti to those ports. Fortunately, this drop in
transshipment traffic was compensated by a shift of Ethiopian traffic in May 1998, from Assab Port in
Eritrea to Djibouti due to a further deterioration in relations between Ethiopia and Eritrea.
Simultaneously, officials at the Port of Djibouti recognized the future strategic importance of Djibouti as
a transit center for goods destined for countries in the Horn of Africa and the need to focus on the transit
rather than the transshipment market. As a result, traffic overall at Djibouti has increased significantly
from 1.7 million tons in 1997 to over 4 million tons in 1998. The new traffic mix being arguably more
lucrative for the country, since it is likely to provide greater employment opportunities for the local
population. While Ethiopia will look to diversify its trade links to the outside world, Djibouti is likely to
remain the predominant port for Ethiopian goods in the near future. For the Djibouti government to
protect that predominant market share, it will need to ensure the quality of the entire logistics system in
the long run, from dockside to the Ethiopian border.
3.    Transport Corridor Development. Long term options for the development of the Djibouti-
Addis corridor are currently under review by various assistance agencies, including the Agence Francaise
and the European Union. There are several corridor development strategies being considered. One is to
upgrade the existing rail connection, the Chemin de Fer Djibouti - Ethiopian (CDE) between Djibouti
Port and Addis Ababa via the Ethiopian town of Dire Dawa. Since most of the traffic is either
containerizable (most already arrives at the port containerized) or is dry or liquid bulk traffic, and the
origin-destination is of a point-to-point nature (Port to Addis), rail seems to be a reasonable option. A
second option is to construct a high quality road link along the same route as the rail link -- via Ali Sabieh
in Djibouti and Dire Dawa. Finally, the existing route, via Dikhil and Galafi, could be substantially
upgraded and re-built. Whatever strategy is adopted, the corridor development program requires a clearly
specified and phased set of transport development actions. These should encompass both physical
infrastructure and institutional development spanning the port, road, trucking and rail sectors. The
program must be integrated with the transportation planning of all the affected countries in the region,
ensuring that important aspects of transport policy, such as regulations (e.g. axle load limnits, through bills
of lading, etc.) are harmonized. Presently, there is a joint committee established between Djibouti and
124



Ethiopia for this purpose, and it is critical that the Bank and other multi- and bi-lateral aid agencies
support this close cooperation with a coordinated strategy.
4.    The long-term development of a Djibouti-Addis corridor is an important component in the
development of the Djiboutian economy. It would provide Djiboutians with a sustainable development
path focussing on a wide range of employment opportunities from port and rail services, trucking and
freight forwarding, to banking, hotel and entertainment services. This ToR sets out the scope of work, to
be financed under an IDA Credit (the Djibouti - International Road Corridor Rehabilitation Project), for
technical assistance to the Government of Djibouti (GD) in the area of trade related services.
B.    OBJECTIVES OF THE ASSIGNMENT
5.    This technical assistance is to prepare an Action Plan for the Development of Djibouti's Trade
Related Services covering the shipping, ship agency, trucking, freight-forwarding, banking, hotel and
entertainment industries in order to enhance the value added services provided to transit traffic between
the Port of Djibouti and its east-African neighbors, and thereby maximize local employment opportunities
related to this traffic.
C.  SCOPE OF WORK
6.    Specifically, the work to be carried out under this assignment will include the following:
(a)   review of the present industry structure, finances, quality/coverage of services, and
employment in the shipping, ship agency, freight-forwarding, trucking, banking, hotel
and entertainment industries;
(b)    analyze key components of transit traffic by commodity type, origin-destination,
ownership and parcel sizes, and assess the efficiency of transit with respect to
costs/delays to cargo within Djibouti;
(c)   identify critical constraints to improved services in each of the industries under
consideration and recommend a program of actions covering regulatory reforms, training
of personnel, and development of necessary institutional arrangements; and
(d)    examine key constraints to private sector investment and expansion in each of the
industries under consideration and recommend on needed incentives/relief which the
Government may provide to stimulate private participation in the transit industry.
125



DJIBOUTI: INTERNATIONAL ROAD CORRIDOR REHABILITATION PROJECT
A UDIT OF PROJECT FINANCIAL STATEMENTS,
SPECIAL ACCOUNT AND ACCOMPANYING SOEs
Terms of Reference
A.    OBJECTIVE
1.    The objective of the audit of the Project Financial Statement (PFS) is to enable the auditor to
express a professional opinion on the financial position of the International Road Corridor Rehabilitation
Project at the end of each fiscal year, and of the funds received and expenditures for each accounting
period as reported by the PFS, as well as an opinion on the Statement of Expenditures.
2.    The project accounts (books of account) provide the basis for preparation of the PFS and are
established to reflect the financial transactions in respect of the project, as maintained by the project
implementing agency.
B.    SCOPE
3.    The audit will be carried out in accordance with International Standards of Auditing, and will
include such tests and controls as the auditor considers necessary under the circumstances. In conducting
the audit, special attention should be paid to the following:
(a)     All external funds have been used in accordance with the conditions of the relevant
financing agreements, with due attention to economy and efficiency, and only for the
purposes for which the financing was provided. Relevant financing agreements are
detailed in the Project's Credit Agreement;
(b)     Counterpart funds have been provided and used in accordance with the relevant financing
agreements, with due attention to economy and efficiency, and only for the purposes for
which they were provided;
(c)     Goods and services financed have been procured in accordance with the relevant
financing agreement;
(d)     All necessary supporting documents, records, and accounts have been kept in respect of
all project ventures, including expenditures reported via SOEs or SAs. Clear linkages
should exist between the books of account and reports presented to the Bank;
(e)     Where Special Accounts have been used, they have been maintained in accordance with
the provisions of the relevant financing agreement; and
(f)     Project accounts have been prepared in accordance with consistently applied International
Accounting Standards and give a true and fair view of the financial situation of the
project at the end of each fiscal year, and of resources and expenditures for the year
ended on that date.
126



C.     PROJECT FINANCIAL STATEMENTS
4.    The Project Financial Statements should include:
(a)    a Summary of Funds received, showing the World Bank, project funds from other donors,
and counterpart funds separately;
(b)    a Summary of Expenditures shown under the main project headings and by main
categories of expenditures, both for the current fiscal year and accumulated to date; and
(c)    a Balance Sheet showing Accumulated Funds of the Project, bank balances, other assets
of the project, and liabilities, if any.
5.    As an annex to the Project Financial Statements, the auditor should prepare a reconciliation
between the amounts shown as "received by the project from the World Bank" and that shown as being
disbursed by the Bank. As part of that reconciliation, the auditor should indicate the mechanism for the
disbursement, i.e. Special Accounts, Statements of Expenditures, or direct reimbursement.
D.    STATEMENTS OF EXPENDITURES
6.    In addition to the audit of the PFS, the auditor is required to audit all SOEs used as the basis for
the submission of withdrawal applications. The auditor should apply such tests and controls as the
auditor considers necessary under the circumstances. These expenditures should be carefully compared
for project eligibility with the relevant financing agreements, and with reference to the Project Appraisal
Document for guidance when considered necessary. Where ineligible expenditures are identified as
having been included in withdrawal applications and reimbursed against, these should be separately noted
by the auditor. Annexed to the Project Financial Statements should be a schedule listing individual SOE
withdrawal applications by specific reference number and amount. Total withdrawals under the SOE
procedure should be part of the overall reconciliation of Bank disbursements described above.
E.    SPECIAL ACCOUNTS
7.    In conjunction with the audit of the Project Financial Statements, the auditor is also required to
audit the activities of the Special Accounts associated with the Project. Special Accounts usually
comprise:
(a)    deposits and replenishments received from the Bank;
(b)    payments substantiated by withdrawal applications;
(c)   interest that may be earned from the balances and which belong to the borrower; and
(d)   the remaining balances at the end of each fiscal year.
8.    The auditor must form an opinion as to the degree of compliance with the Bank's procedures and
the balance of the Special Account at year-end. The audit should examine the eligibility and correctness
of financial transactions during the period under review and fund balances at the end of such a period, the
operation and use of the SA in accordance with the financing agreement, and the adequacy of internal
controls for this type of disbursement mechanism.
127



F.   AUDIT OPINION
9.    Besides a primary opinion on the Project Financial Statements, the annual audit report of the
Project Accounts should also include a separate paragraph commenting on the accuracy and propriety of
expenditures withdrawn under SOE procedures, and the extent to which the Bank can rely on SOEs as a
basis for loan disbursement. The financial statements, including the audit report, should be received by
the Bank no later than six months after the end of the accounting period to which the audit refers. The
auditor should submit the report to the borrower's designated agent rather than to any staff member of the
project entity. The agent should then promptly forward two copies of the audited accounts and report to
the Bank.
G.  MANAGEMENT LETTER
10.   In addition to the audit reports, the auditor will prepare a "management letter," in which the
auditor will:
(a)    Give comments and observations on the accounting records, systems, and controls that
were examined during the course of the audit;
(b)    Identify specific deficiencies and areas of weakness in systems and controls and make
recommendations for their improvement;
(c)    Report on the degree of compliance of each of the financial covenants on the financing
agreement and give comments, if any, on internal and external matters affecting such
compliance;
(d)    Communicate matters that have come to attention during the audit which might have a
significant impact on project implementation; and
(e)    Bring to the borrower's attention any other matters that the auditor considers pertinent.
Due to accelerated expenditures in the project's first year, the auditor will submit a management
letter regarding the P1U' s operations no later than six months after Credit Effectiveness. This will help to
ensure that the PIU's internal controls and operating procedures are satisfactory.
H.    GENERAL
11.   The auditor should be given access to all legal documents, correspondence, and any other
information associated with the project and deemed necessary by the auditor. Confirmation should also
be obtained of amounts disbursed and outstanding at the Bank. Bank Task Managers can assist in
obtaining these confirmations.
12.   It is highly desirable that the auditor become familiar with a copy of the Bank's Guidelines on
Financial Reporting and Auditing of Projects Financed by the World Bank, which summarizes the Banks
financial reporting and auditing requirements. The auditor should also be familiar with the Bank's
Disbursement Manual. Both documents will be provided by the Task Manager.

DJIBOUTI: INTERNATIONAL ROAD CORRIDOR REHABILITATION PROJECT
ESTABLISHING A FINANCIAL MANAGEMENT SYSTEM AND PROCEDURES AT THE PIU
Terms of Reference
A.  BACKGROUND
1.    Djibouti currently serves as the primary transit port for landlocked Ethiopia following the
outbreak of armed conflict between Ethiopia and Eritrea in 1998. Assab, on the Eritrean coast, formerly
assumed this role, but with the sudden shift in 1998 of traffic from Assab to Djibouti Port, the 20-year old
road connection between Djibouti Port and the Addis-Assab Road (via Dikhil and Galafi) was suddenly
required to carry a level of heavy-vehicle traffic it was neither designed for nor in condition to carry.
Portions of the road are presently disintegrating, posing a risk to complete failure on long sections.
2.    The Government of Djibouti (GD) has requested assistance from the International Development
Association (IDA) for a program of emergency road repair of some sections of the national road to
Ethiopia. The objective of this rehabilitation project is to secure unhampered and continued road access
between Djibouti Port and Ethiopia for the next five years. During this five-year period, an Addis Ababa-
Djibouti City long-term corridor improvement scheme is being developed, assessed, and implemented by
the Ethiopian and Djibouti governments with assistance forn the European Union, which is expected to
provide long-term improvements to the corridor.
3.    The IDA project will be implemented by a Project Implementation Unit (PIU), which will be
established within the Ministry of Equipment and Transport. In addition to managing the Project, this
Unit will be in charge of project financial management, including management of all financial
transactions, accounting and reporting activities. The Unit will also manage a Special Account. The PIU
will include financial staff headed by a Accountant reporting to the PITJ's Director General. The
Accountant will launch, with the help of an external consultant, project financial management systems
and procedures which will ensure compliance with Bank guidelines and the timely production of reliable
accounting information on project-related expenditures.
B.    OBJECTIVES OF THE ASSIGNMENT
4.    The objective of the assignment is to design and assist the PIU in establishing a financial control
and accounting system which are in accordance with IDA guidelines (see OP/BP10.02). The system
should reliably record the project's financial operations and activities, produce financial statements and
reports in a timely fashion, and safeguard project assets and resources.
C.  SCOPE OF WORK
5.    The Consultant will work with PIU personnel to develop and implement a project financial
management system on a fast track basis so that the system is operational no later than Credit
Effectiveness (July 31, 2000). As an interim measure, and to avoid delaying Credit Effectiveness, the
project will utilize a manual accounting system, internal control mechanisms and documented operational
policies and procedures as detailed in the following sections. The Consultant must be fluent in French,
and be willing to spend up to one month (continuous) in Djibouti. It is preferable, but not required, that
the Consultant also speaks English.
129



Internal Controls
Internal controls should start with clearly written administrative, accounting and operational
procedures that define levels of authority and responsibilities, ensure an orderly and efficient payment and
procurement process, and properly record and safeguard project-related assets and resources. Specific
attention should be given to establishing:
*  a process to identify and track sources of project financing, including the flow
of funds and the timing of such flows (whether direct to the project or through
government entities);
*  a suitable authorization process for award of contracts and purchase of
equipment and supplies, including documentation procedures;
*  an appropriate segregation of duties and responsibilities, including invoice
processing, accounting duties, and payment functions;
i  design and help implement the use of standard forms for recording and
controlling all transactions;
*  produce an accounting policies and procedures manual in French which
addresses all aspects of financial management, including staffing arrangements
and responsibilities, the flow of funds, internal control procedures, the
accounting system, reporting formats and procedures, and storage of financial
documents; and
*  arrangements for storing project documents and restricting access to authorized
personnel only.
The PIU Director will review and approve all payments before sending the payment request to be
signed by the Minister of Finance or the Secretary General of the MOF. In additional, the PIU will
directly manage a Special Account to be opened at the Banque pour le Commerce et l'Industrie in US
dollars and will be maintained in US dollars only. Procedures to manage and sign on a Special Account
would be communicated and agreed with the Borrower in a disbursement letter to be issued by the Loan
Department.
Accounting System
The accounting system developed for the PIU should reflect project needs and be designed to
provide financial information to all interested parties, including the PIU, the Bank, cofinanciers and
oversight agencies. There should be a linkage between the cost categories used by the accounting
system and the inputs needed to carry out the project. As an interim measure, a manual accounting
system will be utilized until a computerized system is developed and operational, which is expected
about five months after Credit Effectiveness (December 31, 2000). The PIU' s Accountant will be
responsible for establishing the computerized system. The manual system will serve as the foundation
for developing the computerized system, and should:
provide information which is compatible with agreed accounting standards;
130



* permit the establishment of a Chart of Accounts which has a logical structure
for recording accounting transactions, is based on the project's budget, and has
the capacity to classify and sub-classify accounting data;
* facilitate the development of a budgeting system, including planned allocation
of resources, which would be coordinated with the financial accounts in order
to reconcile budget variances with financial figures;
.  summarize accounting balances by source (World Bank or counterpart),
category (works, goods or services), and project component;
* record individual transactions by vendor;
* allow for transfers and adjustments between accounts;
* assist the user to process and maintain Statements of Expenditure (SOEs); and
 provide financial data to measure project performance and create audit trails.
Accounting Standards
In the absence of superior national standards, the accounting standards used by the PIU should be
based on International Accounting Standards (LAS). The use of IAS standards helps to ensure consistent
recording of financial data and presentation of financial statements, and greatly facilitates interpretation of
the information presented.
Records Management
Generally, the management of records should provide a paper trail on which the accounting system
is based, and verification of financial transactions. For each financial transaction, an individual record
should be created. Records management should include:
* clearly defined procedures for creating and maintaining records;
* adequate backup procedures;
* the storage of physical financial records under lock and key and safe from
environmental risks (fire and water damage); and
* easy access for authorized personnel only.
Reporting
The financial management system should be capable of producing a full array of financial
statements and reports, including:
balance sheets, sources and uses of funds, cash flow statements, and notes to
the financial statements; and
131



quarterly Project Management Reports (PMRs) as defined under the Cash
Model (see Annex 7, Project Financial Management Manual).
D.  SCHEDULE
6.    The PIU plans to appoint a project accountant no later than June 30, 2000. Once on board, the
accountant would work closely with the Consultant to develop and implement a financial management
system for the project according to the work plan on the following page. Prior to the accountant's
appointment, it is envisaged that the Consultant will begin developing the foundation of the financial
management system before traveling to Djibouti. The Consultant must be willing to spend up to one
month (continuous) in Djibouti beginning on or about June 30, 2000.
132
